Public Telegram 79

Telegram from Chongqing, reported to the Shanghai News: Recently, we heard that the Ministry of Communications is going to significantly increase postal rates again, which is extremely shocking. It has been found that the previous increase in postage for registered and regular letters by one cent has already burdened the common people. Now, suddenly, another two cents are being added to each, and the postage for printed books is being doubled or even tripled, making it even more difficult for the common people to obtain books. This is detrimental to education and cultural development. Moreover, the purpose of postal services is to facilitate communication, not to make profits. Therefore, postal rates in various countries around the world are light, such as in the United States, where the postage for regular letters has remained at only two cents since the founding of the country and has never been increased. However, in our country, it is increasing again and again, which is contrary to the original intention of establishing postal services. Post offices in our country have been profitable for many years and have not suffered losses, so there is no reason to increase prices. We urge you to withdraw the order and maintain a line of life for education and culture. We are extremely anxious and await your orders. Submitted by Chongqing Commercial Press, China Bookstore, World Bookstore, Chongqing Bookstore, and 25 other bookstores.

Important News

The CER 80

Japanese Train Derails

Japanese Military Believes CER Must Be Held Responsible

Japanese Government Urgently Increases Troops to Defend Against Russia

Self-Defense Army Seizes the Opportunity to Recapture Fangzheng

Harbin Correspondence: Regarding the derailment of a Japanese troop train on the Harbin-Suifenhe section of the CER near Cheng Gaozi Station on the night of the 12th of this month, the details are as follows:

The 23rd Company of the Infantry Battalion of the 39th Regiment, part of the Japanese Murakami Brigade, was returning to Harbin from Wugimi on a troop train at 5:00 PM on the 12th. The entire train consisted of 41 cars. In addition to the ten or so cars for soldiers, the remaining cars were used by about 200 Korean residents, both men and women, and were loaded with military supplies, automobiles, gasoline, and other items. Around 10:50 PM on the 12th, the train was traveling to a place called "Wan De Hao", about 953 kilometers from Harbin, between Xiangfang Station and Cheng Gaozi Station. The roadbed there was high and steep, and as the train was traveling downhill, someone had preemptively removed the bolts on the left side of the track. As soon as the train reached that spot, there was a loud crash from the locomotive, and immediately, 16 cars, including passenger and freight cars connected to the locomotive, derailed and rolled off a 20-foot embankment. The first five passenger cars were immediately crushed. Because one of them was carrying gasoline and another was carrying munitions, they exploded and caught fire after being crushed. Because of the strong wind, the flames were very fierce. Japanese Captain Asazuma, along with Lieutenant Kami, 12 soldiers, were crushed by the cars and burned to death. The rest crawled out of the broken iron and wood, but most were injured. The Russian guards on the train also sustained minor injuries. The train crew used the telephone on a roadside pole to contact Harbin and report the incident to the Japanese military. The Japanese dispatched an emergency train from Harbin to rescue. When the emergency train arrived, black smoke was still rising. Most of the bodies of the Japanese soldiers had been reduced to ashes. It took a long time to rescue the 27 seriously injured and transport them back to Harbin. The next day, an airplane went to scout for traces related to the incident, but found nothing. At noon, the CER dispatched an investigation car with senior road personnel to investigate. After transferring the undamaged cars onto the tracks and repairing the tracks, traffic was restored at 4:00 PM. While the Japanese soldiers were carrying out rescue work that day, a Chinese person passed by the area and was captured by the Japanese soldiers, tied to a telephone pole, and severely beaten, accused of being involved in the track removal. Later, he was taken to Harbin and detained. His fate is still unknown. Since this incident, the Japanese Ministry of the Army sent an urgent telegram to the commander of the Japanese division in Harbin, Domon, ordering him to investigate the true attitude of the Russian side of the CER towards Japan. At the same time, the Kwantung Army Headquarters in Shenyang also sent several specialists to Harbin on the 13th to conduct an investigation, recognizing that the matter was extremely important. On the afternoon of the 13th, Doihara, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Harbin, visited the Russian director of the CER to explain that the Japanese side had entrusted all transportation responsibilities, including the bearing of transportation costs, to the CER. Now that this tragic incident has occurred, the CER must take responsibility. The Russian director agreed that the Russian deputy directors and the head of the engineering department of the railway bureau would form an investigation committee to conduct an investigation. Doihara did not express his opinion, saying that it was not yet the time to negotiate and left. The Russian director then issued a statement in the afternoon, saying: "Regarding the discovery of an explosive device 945 kilometers away by Chadaofu on the 12th, the insurance area member Fan, and the employees Marazov, the district chief and his other colleagues, the road police officers, etc. went to investigate and remove it, resulting in the suspension of traffic between Harbin and Cheng Gaozi for three hours. Afterwards, it was determined that there was nothing unusual on the route between Harbin and Cheng Gaozi. According to the investigation by the rescue train, the derailment was caused by the first and four third-class passenger cars falling off the cliff and eleven freight cars derailing. The cause of the derailment was the removal of railroad bolts, etc."

The Japanese side believed that this type of statement was irresponsible. However, since this incident occurred, the Japanese have been actively engaged in military actions. The Second Division of the Kwantung Army will definitely not return home at the end of its term, and the 10th Division will be transferred from the country and landed in Dalian on the 15th. It is expected to arrive in Harbin around the 20th. Before the new troops arrive, the Japanese army had originally concentrated in Harbin to avoid traces of the League of Nations investigation team. At this moment, the plan to concentrate in Harbin for military importance was immediately canceled. The Murakami Brigade is scheduled to depart for Yimianpo on the 15th to set up defenses. The Amano Brigade is scheduled to be stationed in Heilongjiang on the 16th. The Suzuki Brigade, stationed in Heilongjiang, is scheduled to depart for the Harbin-Manzhouli line on the 18th, with the aim of securing the strategic points of Boketu and Xing'anling. After the 10th Division arrives, it will continue to advance towards the Harbin-Suifenhe and Harbin-Manzhouli lines. The headquarters of the two divisions will also be set up at important points on the east and west lines. The Japanese army is almost in a state of panic.

Since Li Du's Self-Defense Army saw that the Japanese army was in a state of panic, he ordered Chen Dongshan's regiment to cooperate with Liu Wankui's Salvation Army to attack Fangzheng County on the evening of the 13th. They immediately entered while the Japanese army was unprepared and burned four Japanese planes because they could not take off in time. The Japanese army, led by Hasebe, cooperated with the bandit army of Shencheng and retreated to Gaoli Maozi. Fangzheng was thus recaptured by the righteous army. Although Yilan has been bombed for days and the town hall and radio station have been destroyed, the base of the Self-Defense Army has been moved to Fujin, and the radio station has also been moved there, communicating normally since the 12th. Ma Zhanshan sent a telegram from Heihe to Li Du on the 12th, saying that he had safely arrived in Heihe and that his troops were in order and would not return to the province for the time being. The Heilongjiang army has been concentrating towards the lower Jiang Tangyuan area, so the Japanese believe that Ma and Li Ding are cooperating to resist Japan again. The Salvation Army on the Harbin-Suifenhe line has advanced to Gaoling Station. The Xi Qia bandit army has fled at the sound of the wind. Wherever the Salvation Army goes, they can maintain military reputation and are extremely loved by merchants and civilians. Above Hengdaohezi, there are 50,000 International Communist Army Red Guards who recently advanced to the Sandao Dongzi bordering Suifenhe. All sides are filled with anti-Japanese voices. The Russo-Japanese war is getting closer and closer. (14th)

Between Japan and Russia

The Beginning of Hostility 81

Soviet Russia's Plot to Destroy the CER Has Ulterior Motives

Japanese Plane Stolen, Japanese Army Hastens to Deploy Defenses

Russia Increases Troops to the Far East to 150,000

Harbin Correspondence: Two shocking pieces of news have emerged here in the past two days. One is that the Second Songhua River Railway Bridge on the Harbin-Changchun line of the CER was almost blown up, which was later proven to be the work of Soviet railway workers. The other is that a Japanese plane stationed in Harbin was stolen by a Red Russian worker and flown to Russia. The occurrence of these two events and the active military preparations of the Soviet Union in the Far East are sufficient to prove that the relationship between Japan and Russia is deteriorating day by day. The situation is described as follows:

The Second Songhua River Bridge was located between the Laoshaogou and Taolazhao stations on the Harbin-Changchun line. It was built in the 18th year of the Republic of China at a cost of more than 3 million gold rubles and was the second largest project of the CER. At 2:00 AM on the 9th of this month, six or seven Russians secretly walked on the ice from the north bank of the river to the foot of the bridge. Two people held hand-held machine guns, and the rest held box cannons. They placed explosives, five poods (about 150 pounds), under the eighth and ninth piers. While they were working, a White Russian road patroller saw them and was killed. The soldiers guarding the bridge heard gunshots and saw several figures under the bridge and opened fire. The soldiers guarding the gun emplacements at both ends of the bridge also came out to assist. The Russians fled in a panic. A person named Panasevich was captured because he fell behind. A CER employee certificate and important secret code documents were found on his body. Later, two li of detonating cord and 60 pounds of explosives and a pistol were found in the forest on the shore. In addition, there were several kinds of dry rations. Because of this incident, trains coming to Harbin from Changchun were blocked for seven hours before traffic was restored. On the afternoon of the 9th, the Japanese military police went to investigate and arrested more than ten Red Russian CER employees at the Taolazhao and Songhua River stations and sent them to Changchun for interrogation. The Japanese side declared that it had fully proven that this incident was a Soviet plot to disrupt Japanese military transportation plans. It was also reported that after this incident, the Japanese side arrested about forty or fifty Red Russian road workers, who were detained and sent to Changchun for interrogation. Although there was no confirmed confession, it has been proven that it was a planned sabotage operation by Red Russia. Since the Soviet Union had misappropriated the railway property, the CER had become useless and they did not want it to be used for Japanese military advantage, so they tried their best to destroy it. The Japanese were therefore on guard against Red Russia.

Red Russian Worker Steals a Japanese Plane: Regarding the incident of a Red Russian worker stealing a plane, the Japanese had stationed the 9th Independent Flying Squadron at the Nangang Airport in Harbin and employed many Red and White Russian workers to fill the tanks and wash the planes every day. At 5:00 AM on the 8th of this month, a new-style monoplane fighter plane parked at the airport was suddenly piloted by a Red Russian worker and flew rapidly along the Harbin-Suifenhe line. When the Japanese heard the news, they immediately sent four planes to chase after it, but because of the difference in speed, they could not catch up. They chased it to Suifenhe and watched it land at four stations before returning. Because of this incident, the Japanese have been arresting Red Russians for days, but they were secretly suppressed for fear of provoking a Red Russian riot. Currently, three Red Russians have been identified as being related to the plane theft and are being detained in the investigation bureau. At the same time, the headquarters of the Second Division of the Japanese Army has gathered its three brigade troops on the Harbin-Suifenhe line to prevent riots by Red Russians along the line and has stopped its plan to attack Yilan. It is reported that another mixed brigade of the Japanese army will be sent to assist in the defense of the eastern section of the CER within the next few days. The Japanese have already recognized Russia as an enemy.

Soviet Red Army Concentrates in Primorsky Krai: The Soviet Red Army in the Far East is concentrating in the Primorsky Krai, totaling 150,000 troops. Military trains on the Masuri Railway are transporting Red Army troops from the Western Siberia area to the Far East. General Galen, the commander-in-chief of the Red Army, has been recalled to the Military Commission to preside over military orders. His successor, General Putna, has arrived, and the headquarters has been moved to Spassk. In the past week, 10,000 cavalry, artillery, and infantry soldiers have been added to Suifenhe. Thirty planes and fourteen tanks are stationed at four stations. The planes take off and practice every day. Their preparations for a fight with Japan have gradually become apparent. According to Japanese investigations, Russia has been secretly smuggling weapons to the northern border of Korea to support Koreans in their restoration movement. Recently, riots have occurred in North Hamgyong Province. There are also communist workers who go to the eastern line of the CER to incite the Chinese to resist Japan. Plainclothes military spies come and go between Suifenhe and Muling every day, conveying messages. The Far Eastern Red Army has a propaganda team that specializes in propaganda for the war against Japan. They have printed a book called "The Way of the Warrior", which records the strengths and weaknesses of Japanese military equipment. The Bolyi Radio Station broadcasts in Japanese and Korean every night, translating workers' riots and opposition to imperialism. Therefore, the Japanese preparation against Russia is more urgent than against us. It is said that the Second Foreign Fleet's return to Lushun is for this reason. (13th)

Japan Tries Hard to Ease Tensions with Russia

The Japanese Newspaper Says Not to Provoke Major Disputes

The Tokyo Hochi Shimbun said that rumors of deteriorating relations between Japan and Russia have been rampant. The Russian army has been deploying large armies to important areas such as Vladivostok, Khabarovsk, and Blagoveshchensk, with a troop strength of 200,000. The Vladivostok government is actively purchasing food from Manchuria, gradually revealing its preparations for war against Japan. It also incites soldiers and bandits in Manchuria to resist Japan. It is still difficult to predict the future of Japan and Manchuria. However, after the Manchurian Incident, Russia suddenly published the documents exchanged between Japan and Russia, and the seriousness of the situation is already difficult to conceal. Russia's interests in the Far East are the same as those of our country. Now Manchuria, which is the lifeline of Japan, and Russia's Far East interests have become incompatible. Therefore, our country's Far East policy has been restrained by Russia. Therefore, our country cannot tolerate the existence of Russia in northern Manchuria. However, once Japan and Russia turn against each other, Russia will definitely use fierce means against us. At this time, our country should be extremely cautious and not provoke major disputes. Because today our country is deeply unfavorable in the international situation, if the sympathy of the great powers is concentrated on Russia, our country will inevitably be in a state of isolation. The most worrying thing is that if the power factions in Manchuria change their attitude and show goodwill to Russia, a major problem will fundamentally occur in our country's policy towards Manchuria.

The Japanese Shanghai Daily in this port said that the Labor-Peasant Representative Department issued strong remarks in Geneva yesterday. Our (Japanese) Army authorities issued the following statement regarding the expression of Labor and Peasants: Recently, the Soviet powerful news service regarded the train derailment incident in northern Manchuria as a conspiracy by the Japanese military department to expand the scope of the dispute so that the Japanese army could increase its troops in northern Manchuria. However, our military department is still cautious in order to maintain peace in the Orient.

Xiong Xiling Writes to Director Wang to Refute False Accusations 82

Wang Said That the Twenty-One Demands Were Countersigned by Xiong

Xiong Corrects Based on Facts, Hoping That Wang Will Not Be Misled

Ping News: Xiong Xiling recently sent a letter to Wang Jingwei, Director of the Executive Yuan: Director Jingwei, Greetings. Yesterday, I saw in the "World Daily" of the 14th of this month that Director Wang of Luoyang Zhen issued a report at the Central Memorial Week meeting, saying that Xiong Xiling and others were guilty of past crimes and would be severely punished. Also, according to a letter from a friend in Luoyang, Director Wang said in the report at the Memorial Week meeting that the Twenty-One Demands to Japan in 1915 were signed by Yuan Shikai and countersigned by Xiong Bing-san, a member of the current National Crisis Conference, who is still in Shanghai. If he arrives here, we will kill him. I was very surprised when I read this. I remember meeting Mr. Tang Shaoyi in Shanghai in 1919 of the Republic of China. Mr. Tang said, "Mr. Bingsan, you and I are both sinners of the Republic of China." At that time, I deeply admired Mr. Tang's broad and enlightened attitude as a great politician, and the older generation's habit of taking the blame was unattainable. Since I once participated in the government of the Republic of China, I have deeply realized the evil of politics and political parties. Therefore, for the past sixteen years, I have lived in seclusion in the forest and engaged in social work, hoping to avoid wronging the country in my conscience. However, I cannot help but correct the section of what you said about the Twenty-One Demands being countersigned by me, because 1915 was the fourth year of the Republic of China. I had already resigned as Prime Minister of the State in March of the third year of the Republic of China, more than a year ago. Who was the person who countersigned it? You can check the government gazette to know the mistake. At this time of serious foreign negotiations, you are both a political leader and responsible for the survival of the entire country. It seems that you need to carefully review the archives and be cautious. If there is the slightest negligence, you will inevitably harm the country. The accusation of falsely accusing people and wanting to kill them is a minor matter. Although I have sworn sixteen years ago that I will never engage in politics or join any party, I will still be consistent with the government out of my patriotic conscience in the face of this national crisis, and I am willing to be as loyal as Yue Wu Mu. I dare to be loyal and advise you to be clear about it. I also wish you peace, Xiong Xiling, April 16.

Liu He Meets in Xinyang 83

Jointly Discussing Bandit Suppression in Henan and Hubei

Hankou Correspondence: Liu Zhenhua, Pacification Commissioner of the Henan, Shanxi, and Shaanxi Border Area, and Zhang Fang, Commander-in-Chief of the 20th Route Army, needed to discuss the issue of jointly suppressing border bandits in Henan, Hubei, Shaanxi, and Sichuan with He Cheng-jun, the Pacification Commissioner stationed in Hubei, so they traveled from Nanyang and Huangchuan to Xinyang and arrived in Hankou at dawn on the 17th. Concrete measures for bandit suppression in Henan and Hubei were discussed. They were about to return to their respective defenses when Liu Zhi, the Pacification Commissioner stationed in Henan, arrived in Xinyang on patrol on the 19th and sent a telegram inviting He to meet. He then took Liu, Zhang, and He Jingwu, Director of the Pinghan Railway Administration, and others north by car on the 20th. It was heard that after He and others arrived in Xinyang, they would discuss the results of the bandit suppression negotiations in Hankou with Liu Zhi in detail again. He stayed in Xin for a day or two before returning to Hankou. Liu, Liu, and Zhang also returned to their respective defenses after Xin was separated. When He and others went north, they made a statement to the press. He said, "The national crisis is severe, and the bandits are rampant. The first priority is to stabilize the country. The bandits in the border areas of Hubei and Henan use the terrain to exploit each other. They have not been eliminated for many years because the suppression has not been unified. This trip is in response to the invitation of Director Liu Jingfu to discuss the bandit suppression plan and will return to Hankou in a day or two." Liu said, "Director He went to Xin to discuss the bandit suppression matters in the two provinces with Director Liu and others. No meetings will be held, and the date of the joint suppression has not yet been determined." Zhang said, "The redization of southern Henan is very deep. We are currently implementing both suppression and appeasement. After the consultation between Directors He and Liu, the future can be more optimistic. It has been decided to move the refugees in Shangcheng to the counties north of the Yellow River according to the plan I proposed in the 18th year, with three to five hundred people settled in each county. The Henan Provincial Government has allocated 20,000 yuan to handle this matter." According to Ma Lingfu, the chief counselor of the Henan, Shanxi, and Shaanxi Border Area Pacification Commissioner's Office, this time Supervisor Liu and Commander-in-Chief Zhang came to Hankou to discuss the plan for the joint suppression in the four provinces of Hubei, Henan, Shaanxi, and Sichuan with Director He. A decision has been made on the joint suppression of Hubei and Henan, but the deployment of troops and the funding still need to be discussed in Xin. On the other hand, the authorities in Sichuan and Shaanxi were telegraphed to send troops to assist in the suppression, so as to eliminate them all at once. (April 20)

Relief Efforts in Northern Anhui Province Involve Selling Relief Wheat 84

Delayed Distribution of Emergency Relief Stirs Resentment

A dispatch from Bengbu reports that last winter, the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, recognizing the extraordinarily severe disaster situation in northern Anhui, specifically allocated 6,730 tons of American wheat for emergency relief. Later, another 1,200 tons were allocated specifically for work relief. Before long, the Shanghai war erupted, and transportation was disrupted. Only a small amount of relief wheat arrived, causing delays in distribution. To address the emergency, the committee decided to convert some of the American wheat into cash in Shanghai so that funds could be disbursed simultaneously. Moreover, to ensure comprehensive consideration and oversight, local relief officials were strictly prohibited from arbitrarily altering the price of relief wheat to prevent corruption. However, after the relief wheat arrived in Bengbu, the Northern Anhui Relief Office actually sold 2,000 tons of it to the Mai Xing Flour Mill. This caused widespread resentment. Northern Anhui is a wheat-consuming region with mills everywhere. If the suffering people could receive relief wheat, they could grind it into flour and survive, regardless of its quality. Unexpectedly, the emergency relief that was supposed to have been provided last winter has been delayed until now. Only half of the relief wheat has been distributed, and 2,000 tons of it have been sold to the flour mill. It is said that the selling price was a little over 82 yuan per ton, which is about 4,000 yuan less than the price in the interior for every hundred tons. The loss from the 2,000 tons is estimated to be about 80,000 yuan. When the Northern Anhui Relief Office distributed relief supplies to various counties, they were stingy with the relief wheat but insisted on providing cash. Moreover, each county received tens of catties less per ton of wheat. As a result, public opinion was in an uproar. Furthermore, representatives from sixteen counties recently went to Bengbu to request relief wheat, planning to quickly transport it back and distribute it. However, the Northern Anhui Office insisted on issuing cash instead of wheat. The representatives argued that the interior lacked food supplies and that even with cash, it would be difficult to save lives. They were forced to use the funds they received to purchase sorghum, wheat, or flour in Bengbu and transport it back to the disaster areas. Consequently, everyone said that the office was using the disrupted transportation of wheat as an excuse to sell it. Why was it that the transportation of flour, wheat, and sorghum purchased by the counties was not disrupted? Moreover, selling relief wheat in Bengbu wasted time and money, causing the disaster areas to suffer even greater losses. Also, the relief representatives from various counties believed that the local officials in charge of relief were mismanaging the process, delaying relief efforts, and were suspected of colluding to embezzle relief funds. Under the weight of their grievances, they also pleaded with the Northern Anhui Flood Relief Association to uphold justice and advocate for the more than seven million disaster victims based on the facts. After receiving the report, the Relief Association has submitted a report to the Shanghai National Government Flood Relief Committee, requesting that it issue a telegram ordering the Northern Anhui Relief Office to promptly and diligently handle the transportation and storage of goods in order to save the disaster victims. (19th)

Local News 85

Water Police Patrol and Capture Bandits – Songjiang Dispatch: Since the outbreak of the Shanghai war, bandits in various places have been gradually plotting to engage in criminal activities. The Taihu gang of bandits has also taken the opportunity to sneak into the coastal ports of Songjiang and Jinshan, specializing in kidnapping. In addition to deploying additional patrol boats at strategic points in his defense area, Fan Guozhong, captain of the first team of the Water Police of the Provincial Public Security Force, personally led patrol officers Zhong Changfa and others on patrol boats along the coast on the 14th. On the 17th, in the Caojing area, they learned that Qin Bangbei, Wang Shide, Zhou Ziyuan, and other Anhui bandit leaders wanted by the Jiangxi and Zhejiang authorities were hiding there. They immediately surrounded and captured them without making a sound and took them back to the team headquarters for preliminary interrogation. According to Qin Bangbei, he had committed many crimes in the jurisdiction of the second and third districts of the Water Police. Because he was wanted by Jiangxi and Zhejiang, he was temporarily hiding in his hometown. Wang Shide also frankly admitted to committing multiple robbery cases. He said that since he had been captured, he should be executed quickly. Zhou Ziyuan confessed that he was also known as Shaoming and that he had robbed a ship in the Yuhui area, taking 840 yuan. Captain Fan, considering the importance of the bandits, immediately dispatched officers to escort the three men to the Minhang District Headquarters for legal proceedings.

A Deadly Robbery Occurs in Dongdun Town – Gaoyou Dispatch: The Daxing Grain Store, owned by merchant Zhang Bao from Dongdun Town, about fifteen li northeast of Gaoyou City, was suddenly attacked by six bandits armed with guns on the night before last. The store employees immediately fled through the back door to report to the owner. Zhang's eldest son, Youfu, led his younger brother to the store and saw that the bandits had already robbed the store and fled, firing their guns along the way as a warning. Youfu and his brother followed in pursuit for less than a li and managed to capture one bandit. The three of them wrestled together and fell into the river, drowning together. Zhang Bao reported the case to the county yesterday, stating that the money in his store had been robbed by the bandits and that both of his sons had been killed. He requested a strict investigation and arrest of the criminals. Smugglers Import Large Quantities of Japanese Goods – Zhenjiang Dispatch: Since the cessation of hostilities in Shanghai, large quantities of Japanese goods have been imported through Shanghai. Merchants in various ports along the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway have also taken the opportunity to purchase goods. Recently, it was reported that a package with the number 4537 was sent from Changzhou Qiantai Chang to Gaozi Heji, containing Japanese goods. It was also reported that a large number of Japanese goods from a certain Zhenjiang merchant would arrive within a few days. The Zhenjiang Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has secretly dispatched inspectors to the riverside station to intensify surveillance.

Cheng Tianfang Sworn in as President of Zhejiang University – Hangzhou Dispatch: Shao Peizi, the president of National Zhejiang University, requested to resign from his position. After approval, the Ministry of Education announced the appointment of Cheng Tianfang as his successor. After accepting the appointment, Cheng arrived in Hangzhou in late March. The university's monthly expenses were 65,000 yuan, with 30,000 yuan allocated by the central government and the remainder subsidized by Zhejiang Province on a monthly basis. After the Shanghai Incident, the central government accumulated arrears for three months, and Zhejiang Province also experienced arrears in payments to various agencies for several months, causing considerable difficulties. Therefore, Cheng and Zhou Junyan, the director of the Zhejiang Finance Department, met to discuss ways to raise funds. Cheng then went to Beijing to personally report the difficulties. The Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance agreed to allocate some funds to maintain operations. Cheng returned to Hangzhou from Beijing and held a swearing-in ceremony in the university auditorium at 8:00 a.m. yesterday (the 21st). Chen Bu** was sent by the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education to supervise the ceremony. Li Peien, Xu Shaodi, and forty other people attended. After the ceremony, President Cheng was sworn in. Then, Chen, representing the central government, delivered a speech. Guests such as Yang Mianzhong gave speeches. Cheng's response included three key points: university education should include (1) character education, (2) academic education, and (3) vocational education. He took office in the afternoon.

Qingpu Organizations Request Rent Exemption: The Jiangsu Provincial Government, due to heavy administrative expenses and insufficient budget, issued a notice to all counties to collect two months' rent to supplement funds. After receiving the order, the Qingpu administrative authorities began investigating and implementing the policy. However, due to the severe damage caused by last year's floods and the economic devastation caused by the recent invasion of the Japanese, various people's organizations have sent telegrams to the province requesting a halt to the rent collection. It is reported that Qiu Shaoxian, Dai Yiqun, Zhang Ziyi, and 240 other members of the Qingpu Shanghai Fellow Association have also jointly telegraphed the province, appealing for the revocation of the order.

Famine-Stricken People Cause Disturbances in Changshu – Changshu Dispatch: Famine-stricken people in the Fushan area of this county, due to last year's famine and the recent lack of production, have gathered to cause disturbances. The authorities, recognizing the hardship of the farmers, did not want to suppress them. However, the disturbances have become more intense, with incidents of people gathering to rob rice and beat others. On the afternoon of the 15th of this month, Wen Genfu, who was a boatman from He Cai Town, happened to be at home when he saw a group of more than a thousand famine-stricken people approaching. When he tried to stop them, he was beaten. He was covered in blood and on the verge of death. He was carried to his boat and sent to the Jishan Hospital in the city for treatment. It is reported that his life is in danger. At the same time, eight or nine other people were seriously injured in the area.

Women Xia Ma and Others Should be Prosecuted as Traitors 88

Enticing Women to Jiading

To Provide Pleasure to the Heinous Japanese Army, the Women Cried and Refused

The Police Have Filed a Lawsuit

Xia Ma, a Ningbo woman residing at a certain address on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, colluded with local resident Ni Ada and Ningbo native Ma Chaonian to entice Chinese women to work as hostesses at a newly established wine shop in Yangshupu for a monthly salary of 20 to 30 yuan. From the 18th to the 21st of this month, they deceived women to go to Jiading to provide pleasure to the Japanese army and profit from it. They opened room 16 at the Sanjiang Hotel at 12 North Hai Road and successively tricked women such as Zhang Chen, Zhuo Lin, Huang Zhang, Liu Huang, Liu Gu, and Chen Lu into the hotel to negotiate. The women were unaware of the situation and agreed to go to work. At noon on the 20th, Xia Ma borrowed a car and went to meet with Bao Yunmo, a Japanese man, at 132 Kaobazi Road. Ma Chaonian acted as the interpreter, falsely claiming that the women needed to be examined by a doctor in Yangshupu to determine if they were suitable for employment. Two cars were hired, and six other women went along. Unexpectedly, they drove straight to Jiading. After getting out of the car, the women were taken to a Nanyang Hotel to stay. Soon after, plainclothes Japanese men and soldiers came upstairs, teasing the women and trying to dance with them and commit indecent acts. The women were horrified and realized they had been deceived. They cried and refused. The hotel waiter secretly reported the incident to the nearby Japanese military headquarters, who sent someone to take the women back to Shanghai. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the six women, including Zhang Chen, and Xia Ma were sent back in cars. On the way, they got off at North Sichuan Road, and the women argued with Xia Ma. Detective Xiao Erfu, Chinese detective Liu Decheng, and Chinese constable No. 2762 heard the commotion and inquired about the situation. They took Xia Ma to the Hongkou Police Station. Xia Ma confessed that Ni Ada lived at 27 Zilaihu Street in the French Concession and Ma Chaonian lived at 113 Daqing Lane on Nanjing Road. The police secretly arrested Ni and Ma and detained them separately. Yesterday morning, lawyer Zhang Tianyin of the First Special District Court presented the case and requested a trial. Zhang Chen and the other six women testified about what happened and confronted Xia Ma, Ni Atai, and Ma Chaonian. Their statements were evasive. Bao Yunmo, a Japanese man residing at 132 Kaobazi Road, claimed to be in the coal business and had known Ma Chaonian for four years. He said that because many young soldiers in the Jiading army liked women, he entrusted Ma Chaonian to find them. Judge Shen Bingrong ordered the three defendants to remain in custody pending sentencing.

Traffic in the Southern City to be Cut Off from 7 PM

Yesterday was the birthday of Lenin, the deceased leader of the Russian Communist Party. The Chinese and concession authorities in Shanghai feared that the Communist Party would hold demonstrations. Minutes of the Provisional Meeting of the Zhejiang Private Electricity Association 94

The Zhejiang Private Electricity Association held a provisional meeting at 25 Central Road, 3rd floor, in this port on the afternoon of the 21st of this month. More than forty representatives from various companies, including Li Yanshi, Ye Yangwu, Han Yimin, Yang Yunong, Li Shuxiong, Gao Luqun, and Yang Boan, elected Han Yimin as chairman. The agenda included (1) the situation of Zhejiang Province collecting national crisis donations and the association's petition to Hangzhou, as well as the investigation of the national crisis donation situation for various industries. For example, the Zhejiang Telegraph Bureau claimed that the Ministry ordered that telegraph fees be charged uniformly throughout the country, and Zhejiang could not be an exception. No tariffs were charged on Shanghai-Hangzhou trains and long-distance telephones. To show consideration for public officials, the Provincial Government ordered its subordinates to collect only once, and those below 40 yuan were exempt. The Hangzhou City rent was approved by the Provincial Government to be reduced by 30% of the original amount, starting in April. (2) The Zhejiang business tax was increased to 10 per mille. (3) The Provincial Government's resolution to collect the Yongjia Puhua Electric Light Combustion Education Donation has been submitted to the Executive Yuan Construction Committee by the Association. After Zhejiang Province Government argued reasonably, it resolved that the Provincial Government’s resolution to collect 10% of public utilities for the national crisis donation for a period of one year is about to be implemented. How should we respond? It was resolved that (1) the electricity national crisis donation should be reduced by 5%. (2) The collection period should be extended from one year to two years, but it should be stated that if the national crisis is resolved, the collection should be stopped. (3) State-owned enterprises such as trains and telegraphs should be collected uniformly when they are collected. (4) This special donation is for the national crisis, and other donations should not be used as precedents. (5) The Wuxing Electric Company proposed that electricity users who heard that the national crisis donation would be collected reported the suspension of lights and requested that the lines be cut, reaching 10% of the total amount. How should we provide relief? It was resolved to investigate the situation of various companies and then ask the government to provide relief through the association. The meeting then adjourned.

Urging the Abolishment of Inner Harbor Licenses for Steamships 101

The Ministry Order Has Been Promulgated for Over a Year, Yet the Customs Has Not Complied

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables the Ministry of Communications, Requesting Consultation and Implementation

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Communications yesterday, requesting the implementation of the abolition of special inner harbor licenses for steamships to benefit shipping merchants. The telegram reads: "To Your Excellency, the Ministry of Communications in Luoyang: On the 20th of this month, according to a letter from the Inland Steamship Industry Association, a letter from the Tongyuan Steamship General Bureau, a member of the association, states that there has been a notorious practice of domestic commercial steamships navigating inland rivers being required to exchange for inner harbor licenses. This decree is tantamount to tying one's own hands and feet. Various local industry groups have repeatedly appealed for its abolition, but it has not been approved. It was not until May of last year that Instruction No. 1699 of the Ministry of Communications was received, stating that the association's request to abolish the exchange of special inner harbor licenses for domestic commercial steamships to facilitate shipping merchants, etc., had been approved on April 3rd. Now, after consultation between the Ministry and the Ministry of Finance, it has been decided that henceforth, any domestic vessels that have already been issued a Ministry license may, after verification by the Customs, be exempt from being issued a ship's badge or river port special license and river license to avoid complexity. In addition to the revision of the regulations for the registration and licensing of steamships, which was announced and implemented on the 3rd of this month, this is urgently ordered for your information, etc. Subsequently, on May 11th, various newspapers also revealed a public notice from the Ministry of Communications with the same intention as the instruction. The decree is clear and unambiguous, but the Jianghai Customs, just ten days after the publication of this Ministry order, on May 13th, requested verification of all matters regarding our Bureau's Tongyi small steamer, still according to precedent, and ordered the payment of ten taels of silver for the inner harbor license fee, issuing a receipt as proof. Initially, it was thought that it had not been long since the Ministry of Communications announced this decree abolishing inner harbor licenses, and the Jianghai Customs may not have received instructions from the Ministry of Finance, and therefore had not implemented it. Unexpectedly, afterwards, a total of seven of our Bureau's Flying Cloud, Cun'an, and other steamers requested verification successively, and all were required to exchange for inner harbor licenses, and the license fees collected ranged from twenty taels for larger vessels to five taels for smaller vessels. To this day, they still disregard the laws and regulations that have been consulted and promulgated by the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Finance, and their restrictions on Chinese vessels and obstruction of inland river traffic are unparalleled. A copy of the Ministry of Communications' instruction notice and a receipt for the Jianghai Customs' collection of the inner harbor license fee for our Bureau's Tongyi small steamer have been combined into a film and sent for your review. We request that your association forward a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it submit it to the Ministry of Communications for approval to consult with the Ministry of Finance to order the Jianghai Customs that inner harbor licenses, which have long been explicitly abolished, must not be exchanged in violation of the order, and license fees must not be collected, in order to respect the law, etc." Upon arriving at the meeting, it was thought that this notorious practice of inner harbor licenses, which harms merchants and afflicts the people, has already been abolished by a Ministry order and should no longer exist. The Jianghai Customs has been ordered for nearly a year, but has delayed implementation without knowing why. Therefore, we dare to send this letter with the facts and attach a photography, and humbly request your association to submit it to the Ministry of Communications for approval to consult with the Ministry of Finance to order the Jianghai Customs that these inner harbor licenses, which have already been explicitly abolished, must not be continued, and license fees must not be collected, in order to comply with the law and benefit transportation. This is for the public good, etc. Upon arriving at the meeting, it was found that steamships only need to have a Ministry license to be allowed to navigate, and there is no need for the Customs to issue ship badges or river port special licenses and river licenses. This is in accordance with Instruction No. 1699 of Your Ministry, and Announcement No. 1 was issued by Your Ministry on May 11th of last year. This case has been promulgated for nearly a year, so why do the affiliated Customs offices still resist implementing the Ministry order and still issue licenses and collect fees? Furthermore, according to Announcement No. 1 of Your Ministry, this case was originally submitted by the Inspector General of Customs, so the Customs offices have no excuse to secretly obstruct it. The previous situation in the letter is even more surprising. It is reasonable to cable Your Ministry for review and approval, and to immediately consult with the Ministry of Finance to notify the Jianghai Customs and other Customs offices throughout the country to strictly comply with the case of abolishing special licenses last year, in order to comply with government orders. This is for the public convenience. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows.

New Statistics on Chinese and Foreign Films 102

Chinese Exports Only Account for One-Tenth of Foreign Imports

The Film Censorship Committee, jointly established by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, will compile various statistics on the feature films that have been censored from the time of its establishment (June 1931) to the end of December 1931. (1) The types of feature films censored in 1931 include 823 from the United States, 427 from China, 41 each from France and Germany, 31 from the United Kingdom, and 4 from Russia. The percentages are 60% for the US, 31% for China, 3% each for France and Germany, 2% for the UK, 0.3 for Japan, and 0.1 for Russia. The total number of film types from all countries is 1,368, the total number of reels is 11,814, and the total length in meters is 3,066,280. (2) There are 58 Chinese production companies, with the most being the Star Film Company with 90 films, Great China Lily with 41 films, 5 companies with more than 20 films, and 4 companies with more than 10 films, including Tianyi, Youlian, Fudan, and Great Wall. The rest have less than 10 films. There are 36 foreign production companies, with the US accounting for 19 and producing the most, such as MGM with 203 films, Paramount with 189 films, and Fox with 128 films. There are 6 French companies, 7 German companies, 2 British companies, and 1 each from Japan and Russia. (3) Two out of every three sound films are from the US, accounting for two-thirds of the total. France accounts for one-half, and Germany and the UK each account for one-third. Three out of 200 Chinese films are sound films. (4) In terms of film content, the first category of Chinese films is legends, accounting for 41% of the total, the second is society, accounting for 18%, the third is human interest, accounting for 15%, and the fourth is love, accounting for 11%. The first category of foreign films is love, accounting for 47%, the second is human interest, accounting for 22%, the third is legends, accounting for 10%, and the fourth is society, accounting for 6%. (5) The number of foreign films imported into China is 941, while the number of Chinese films exported is 95, accounting for only one-tenth of foreign films. (6) A total of 63 films were deemed unsuitable for screening and were prohibited, including 37 foreign films and 26 Chinese films.

Tong Sanmao Cannot Escape Criminal Responsibility in the Huang Baiying Suicide Case 106

Probation Can Be Granted If He Is Suffering from an Illness

The Opinion of the Police Lawyer

Last summer, the dancer Huang Baiying was induced by Tong Sanmao to take a car to Wusong for coolness. On the way back, Tong obtained silver dollars from Huang to buy sleeping pills and went to the Cangzhou Hotel. Initially, they planned to commit suicide together. However, after Huang took the poison, she suddenly did not want to die and hired a car to take her to the hospital. After the doctor's rescue, she was able to survive. The police learned of the incident and, after investigation, prosecuted Tong for instigating suicide. The First Special District Court sentenced Tong to two years of imprisonment. Tong refused to accept the judgment and appealed. As a result, the appeal was rejected. Tong then appealed to the Supreme Court, which finally ordered the case to be sent back to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court for retrial in January of this year. This twist has taken a year and a half. Tong contracted lung disease in prison, which has become increasingly serious. He was granted medical parole. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the retrial of the case. Tong and his lawyer arrived on time, but Huang Baiying was not seen because her address had changed and she could not be summoned. Subsequently, Judge Yu and Assessors Zhao and Guo, together with the prosecutor and Secretary Qian Qizhong, took their seats for the trial. First, police lawyer Li Zhishan stated the facts of the case, followed by questioning Tong Sanmao. However, Tong's voice was extremely low due to his illness. The judge believed that the contents of the case had been clarified after several trials, so he briefly questioned him and then ordered the debate to begin. Therefore, the police lawyer stated that the case was prosecuted for the crime of instigating suicide. The first trial believed that the facts were true and the crime was real, so he was sentenced to two years of imprisonment. However, the defendant argued that he intended to die together. After investigating the methods of instigating suicide, there are several types. After reviewing the facts of the case, the defendant used intimidation and verbal stimulation to cause Huang to commit suicide. Although Huang was sent to the hospital afterwards, this cannot be considered a cessation of behavior, but rather a repentance of previous wrongs. Tong has been imprisoned for more than a year and has been ill. If the judge is particularly lenient and grants him probation, it is possible. If he still does not accept criminal responsibility, it is difficult to deny it. Finally, Tong Sanmao's lawyers, Xu Fuji and Liu Shifang, successively defended him. The court ordered the sentence to be pronounced on the afternoon of April 29th.

Yang Shengzhi's Concubine Sues for Inheritance 107

Lawyer Zhang Shizhao Submits a Written Opinion

Yang Shengzhi, a former member of Wang Tianpei's army who rose to the rank of military commander through meritorious service, died of illness on March 21, 1931, leaving behind three concubines and an eight-year-old blind son. The three concubines are Cai Huaxian, the mother of the blind child, Wang Jiazhen, and Hua Xunyang. When Yang was alive, Wang Jiazhen was favored alone, and there was great animosity between her and Cai Hua. After Yang's death, the two women joined forces to exclude Jiazhen, accusing her of adultery, stealing her clothes, refusing to live with her, and cutting off her living expenses, thus forming today's lawsuit. On the fifth day after Yang's death, a meeting of relatives and subordinates was held, and Yan Renshan, the director of the Nanjing Office, handed over a bank deposit slip from the Shanghai Bank of China for 50,000 yuan and three deposit slips from the Zhongnan Bank for a total of 70,000 yuan. It was decided that the deposit slips would be kept by Yang Shengbin, the deceased's younger brother. Subsequently, disputes arose repeatedly in the family, and the deposit slips changed hands and fell into the hands of Cai Huaxian. Later, Shengbin sued and obtained a preliminary injunction from the First Special District Court. Before long, Shengbin and Cai Concubine reconciled and requested the withdrawal of the preliminary injunction. Cai successively went to the two banks and withdrew all the money. Therefore, Wang Jiazhen sued her, resulting in the current lawsuit. The subject of the lawsuit is to demand a one-time alimony payment of 42,000 yuan. Wang is 25 years old this year, and calculating until the age of 60, there are still 35 years. The annual living expenses are estimated at a minimum of 1,200 yuan, so the amount should reach this figure. Wang hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Xiang Xun, while the defendant was represented by lawyer Shan Yuhua. At 11:00 am on the 22nd of this month, Judge Yang Peng appeared in court to try the facts. After Lawyers Xiang and Shan stated the case in turn, Lawyer Zhang separately submitted a written opinion and gave an oral presentation to the judge. The most important points were that the case should take into account the interests of both the plaintiff and the defendant, starting from the protection of the inheritance, and the 120,000 yuan that Cai had already proposed had to be investigated and seized. It was also hoped that the just gentry of Guizhou and those who had friendships with the late military commander Yang would come forward to manage the matter so as to properly handle the aftermath of Yang's death. Judge Yang, based on Lawyer Zhang's opinion of preliminary injunction, questioned the defendant's representative, Lawyer Shan Yuhua, and requested the court to reject the plaintiff's lawsuit. The reason was that Wang Jiazhen and Zhao Ruiqi had been defendants in a criminal case in the Jiangning Local Court. The cause of action was the crime of abduction, theft, and stolen goods. There was Volume 102 of the Jiangning Court's Twentieth Year Zi Case for verification. Moreover, since this case has not yet concluded, alimony cannot be requested according to the valid regulations. Even if there were no criminal incidents, the plaintiff had issued a handwritten receipt for the保管 of 10,000 yuan. The defendant is still requesting the return of this 10,000 yuan in the Jiangning Court. How can she request alimony in the Shanghai Court again? As for the plaintiff's request to apply for a preliminary injunction on the property, but she did not point out the location of the property, how can it be seized? The court ordered the submission of a supplementary statement and rescheduled the hearing. The original written opinion is as follows:

The written opinion of Zhang Shizhao, the lawyer and litigation agent for Yang Wang Jiazhen's alimony pursuit case, is to clarify the main points of the case in order to maintain its benefits and fairness. The purpose of this case is the distribution of the inheritance, and the source of the inheritance is the accumulation of a recently famous senior military officer. Unfortunately, after the death of the military officer, there was only one eight-year-old blind son left, and the rest were concubines. Therefore, the plaintiff, Wang Jiazhen, is the fourth concubine, and the defendant, Yang Xiuqian (i.e., the eight-year-old son), is the mother of the son, and Ji Huaxian is the third concubine, and another Hua Xunyang is the fifth concubine. The bedding is flat, and there is no way to say who is virtuous or who is superior. Judging from the situation, this type of family is notoriously lax in discipline. Once the head of the family dies, there is no hope of common maintenance. After the military officer's death, the chief of staff in Nanjing, Yan Renshan, handed over 70,000 yuan in deposits from the Zhongliang Bank and 50,000 yuan from the Bank of China, totaling 120,000 yuan. No matter how this 120,000 yuan is divided, it is undoubtedly the common property of the three concubines. The three or five concubines usually jealous of the plaintiff, even at this time, they took advantage of her isolation to plot to trap her. Finally, there was a case in the capital. On one side, they quietly settled the case, and on the other side, they successively emptied the two banks in the name of the property inheritor (i.e., her son Xiuqian). The concubines are deeply fond of hardship and have many bad habits. In addition, traitors are coveting everything from the side, and there is no way to be self-reliant. Once the 120,000 yuan is in their hands, they will be free to squander it and be forced by others to divide it. It is expected that it will not take long before it will turn into nothing. At that time, it will not belong to the plaintiff, and there will be no source of funds. Even if the Cai Huaxian and other orphans and widows are poisoned, how can they survive on their own? From the perspective of this lawyer, the focus of this case should be on the overall and permanent interests of the family, and the starting point should be the preservation of the 120,000 yuan deposit (and other real estate by analogy). According to the bank report, this money is withdrawn by the heir in accordance with the bank's practice of finding a guarantee, but whether it is easy to use other accounts and still store it in the original bank or transfer it to another bank (the Bank of China's reply to this lawyer's letter is attached), and whether it is stored as a whole or in part, the court should strictly inquire of the defendant and order him to confess one by one, and then the plaintiff should request a declaration of preliminary execution and give it a lien. If the defendant refuses to confess the truth in the name of civil affairs, the court should also order the defendant to provide cash in the amount of 120,000 yuan, or provide a guarantee with a solid shop to serve as a pawn. The outcome of this case depends entirely on the 120,000 yuan, which is at risk of being lost. Once it is lost, everything will be completely gone. The displacement of the plaintiff and defendant in the future will burden relatives and friends, and all will be in the candlelit count. At that time, the law and human relations will be unable to revive the blind. Even if the above-mentioned traitors are in the court, what will it do? Extending to this, the most important meaning of resolving the unresolved case should be to fully protect the inheritance and leave it for surplus, so that the fair gentlemen of Guizhou and those who are well-versed in the friendship with the military commander who died can handle the overall situation and deal with it in the long term. Even if they retreat and distribute the property by person to the three concubines, they are all women who are loyal to the Yang family, and their status is equal to the law and there is nothing low or high. If the current situation is followed, Cai and Hua will embezzle a large amount of money and spend it at will, causing the plaintiff to be frozen and starved and unable to enjoy the benefits of her late husband's wealth. The feelings of righteousness and justice in the world are nothing more than this. It has been found that the two banks' deposits have been appealed by Yang Shengbin, the younger brother of the deceased military commander, to the court's ruling (Preliminary Judgment No. 97 of the 20th year), which allowed a preliminary injunction. The concubines have also sued each other in the Capital Court, and they have all posted cash bail in each case. It seems that the matter of attachment in this case has been witnessed before and is not an abrupt new meaning. Moreover, this attachment belongs to the fixed common living expenses, which is absolutely slow compared to other commercial funds. The defendant may have made a mistake in his chance. The procedure is extremely simple (that is, the applicant for attachment does not need to provide a guarantee, etc.). The court should resolutely implement this first, and then treat the whole case for investigation and treatment. If the defendant makes use of the inheritance qualification of his eight-year-old blind son to collude with close relatives and embezzle all the inheritance for his own use, he obviously harms the plaintiff's property rights and has already constituted the crime of embezzlement under criminal law with a surplus. If you think about it, the defendant is a muddy woman with a large amount of money in her hands. She dares to disregard the restrictions of litigation, and her whereabouts are secretive and migratory. How can there be no treacherous people to protect and bully her for profit? It is also in the interest of the defendant herself that the court should strictly investigate so that the whereabouts of the 120,000 yuan are clearly understood, and the case will begin to have clues to be found. If this is the case, treating this case from the scope of civil affairs to criminal affairs is the path of national law. The humble opinion is that the military commander died not long after building a tooth. His meritorious service is to the country, so that his family can get what they want and there is no scandal in the family. This is what the meritorious friends and relatives want. Therefore, it is appropriate to treat both sides with equal benefits in the law, and it is appropriate to treat both the living and the dead with the same feelings. This is the reason for writing this book. Only the judge will adopt and implement it, and I will not be able to fulfill my great wish.

This has been approved by the Board of Directors.

Jiang Jingcheng, a tea boy, was taken to the Japanese headquarters by Japanese soldiers for questioning on the first day of this week. Fire on Tangshan Road Kills Elderly Woman 111

At around 1:00 am yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out at No. 29 Yongji Lane, Tangshan Road. An elderly woman from Jiangbei, Shen (75 years old), was burned to death on the spot. The Fire Department's fire truck rushed to the scene to put out the fire. The Huishan Police Department was informed and ordered detectives to investigate. The body of the elderly woman was carried to the Perin Road Autopsy Room. At around 10:00 am, Li Ying, the prosecutor commissioned by the First Special District Court, arrived at the scene to examine the body. According to Zhou Jiguang, the deceased was his mother and lived with him at the front building of the address. The fire was started downstairs at that time. He heard a quarrel downstairs in the hall, where people were gambling on playing cards. He went downstairs to investigate and ran to the lower floor of the stairs, where he saw a fire. They were scrambling to move things out. Although he tried to put water on the fire, it was ineffective. His wife and children also escaped after hearing the alarm. His elderly mother was old and had difficulty walking, so she could not escape in time. The staircase had been burned down at that time, and he could not rescue her either. Li then ordered the examination to determine that the deceased was a female surnamed Shen and had been burned to death before death. The body was handed over to her son, Zhou Jiguang, who signed for it and took it back for coffin and burial.

Murdered Male Corpse on Xietu Road 113

Yesterday morning, a murdered male corpse was found on the ground at the eastern end of Xietu Road, Dapu Road, in West Shanghai. It was discovered by villagers passing by, who reported it to the Second District Police Department. The police sent a police officer to the scene with Gu Zhonglian, the head of the 15th Tu of the 25th Bao. The corpse was found to be around 30 years old, wearing a white cloth short shirt, black pants, and white socks, but no shoes. There was a hemp rope tied around the neck, with a total of two wraps. After searching, no family members came forward to identify the body. The local court was immediately notified to request an autopsy. Shen, the prosecutor, was commissioned to arrive at the scene to examine the body and determined that he had been strangled to death before death. After surveying the area, there were no messy footprints, and the deceased's feet had no shoes, which further proved that he had been murdered and then abandoned. It was then ordered that the body be photographed and collected by the Charity Hall and sealed in a壇 while awaiting the arrest of the murderer and further investigation.

Sha Zhaoping Shoots Bai Yufu 114

The Cause Was Gambling with Sha's Wife

Bai Yufu, 26, from Shandong, lives at No. 638 Bao'an Lane, Gordon Road, Shanghai West. His fellow villager Sha Zhaoping, 24, also lives at No. 186 in the same neighborhood. Both are public bus drivers. They are both Muslims and considered childhood friends. However, Bai had resigned and was at home. Two weeks ago, Bai went to Sha's house to gamble on Pai Gow and suddenly had a quarrel with Sha's wife due to teasing.

Sha was on the side at the time and did not take it seriously. Last night at 11:00 pm, Bai went to Sha's place to chat. After a while, Sha invited Bai to go out to a dark place on Xiaoshadu Road. Sha then took out a pistol from his sleeve and fired two shots at Bai's head. One bullet hit the back of his neck, and Bai immediately ran away in pain, shouting for help. He ran into the Gordon Road Police Station to report the situation. Chinese and Western detectives immediately went to Sha's house to arrest him, but Sha had already fled and disappeared without a trace. The injured person was sent to Baojiang Hospital for treatment by a police car. It is said that the injury was critical and his life may be in danger.

Mistaking Pregnancy for Menstrual Disorder 115

Yang Daoqing's Wife Aborted as a Result

Xia Ziyang is Accused of Homicide

Yang Daoqing, 28, from Yancheng, lives at No. 9, Hengchang Lane, Conti Road, in the French Concession. His wife, Xu, felt unwell on the 10th of this month and went to the clinic of Xia Ziyang, a country doctor from the same village, at No. 12, Bao'an Lane, Bail Road, Nanyang Bridge. After Xia felt her pulse, he diagnosed her with menstrual disorder and prescribed a prescription for Xu to take home and boil. However, he did not know that Xu was three or four months pregnant, and the medicine caused her to have an abortion and become ill. Yang believed that Xia was an incompetent doctor who caused the death of his wife, so he hired a lawyer to file a criminal complaint in the Second Special District Court, accusing Xia of causing an abortion and injury due to professional negligence, and requesting that the case be investigated and that compensation of 3,500 yuan be claimed. The court summoned both parties to the court yesterday afternoon at 3:00 pm for a trial in the third criminal court. First, the plaintiff, Yang Daoqing, stated the previous situation and said that his wife was seriously ill due to the abortion. When questioned, Xia confessed that when the plaintiff's wife came to his clinic for treatment, he inquired in detail and diagnosed her with menstrual disorder, and did not mention that she was pregnant. He also hired lawyer Wang Shizong to defend him and presented his registration certificate from the Health Bureau and the license issued by the French Municipal Council. The court ordered him to deposit 2,000 yuan in cash for bail and wait for a continued hearing at a later date.

Peace and Reconstruction 121

— Ji Ping

The national crisis has become so severe that, although more than half of the populace has been awakened from their slumber, and are making a final struggle at this moment of survival, there are still many who hesitate and stray down the wrong path. Look at the soldiers who hold onto their weapons for self-interest, the merchants who only seek profit, the traitors who act against the tide, and the national thieves who are inclined to cede sovereignty and humiliate the country – they are all still hesitant!

After this painful experience, we deeply feel that the outbreak of this national crisis is not so much the cause of the Japanese invasion, but rather the result of twenty years of internal strife. The brutality of the Japanese is certainly 可根 (detestable), but if our own people did not fight for power and seize territory, and instead worked together with one heart and one mind to build a strong defense for national defense, would the enemy be able to penetrate our territory and seize our throat? Let's not dwell on the past. From now on, all compatriots across the country should move towards the path of [the movement of peace and reconstruction]. However, the so-called [peace] is limited to [internal], not [external]. In other words: [Turn the gun outward] and unite against foreign invaders. This should be the case during this period, and it should be the case forever. How to implement the [peace and reconstruction movement]? This is naturally a very important question. First, all soldiers in the country should thoroughly realize that they should never participate in internal wars again. Second, the entire nation should be organized to supervise [the united action of peace and reconstruction]. Here, I would like to introduce the four methods proposed by Mr. Liu Zhan'en for reference: (1) Establish a national non-war construction pact; (2) Adopt a non-cooperation policy towards those who undermine domestic peace and participate in internal wars; (3) Reward leaders of reconstruction; (4) Emphasize peace and reconstruction propaganda. In addition to these, there are certainly many other methods, but these four points cover a wide range of meanings, and effective regulations can be formulated based on these ideas. For example, the National Crisis Conference passed a National Representative Assembly, and in Shanghai, there is also the initiation of the People's Constitution Advancement Association. If these two groups truly want to take responsibility for saving the country, they urgently need to solve the following two issues

[Implement armed resistance to recover lost territory]

Implement the domestic peace and reconstruction movement

Shanghai Battle and Military Equipment (17) 123

— Yi Zang

Sound detectors. In recent times, with the development of the air force, there is a deep feeling that air defense is more important than anything else. All kinds of air defense equipment have been devised as preparations, such as aerial sound detectors, nighttime searchlights, alarm transmitters, intelligence devices, etc. They have all emerged based on the experience of past wars. Now, let's first talk about the sound detector among the new weapons. This kind of air defense equipment was invented after World War I. Before the war, the only way to detect enemy aircraft was to listen with human ears. During the war, it was impossible to prevent aircraft from ravaging the area. After the war, a Frenchman first created a trumpet-shaped sound receiver that was attached to both ears. However, the structure of this device could not determine the horizontal angle or vertical angle. Therefore, it was not very effective. Later, it was changed to four, but it was still not accurate enough. Before long, a parabolic aerial sound detector was invented, which was slightly more advanced than the trumpet type. However, aircraft travel at a very high speed, and when using a sound detector to determine direction, the position often differs. Therefore, the time for sound wave transmission was further modified. Later, with the help of electrical linkage devices, six improvements were made. The most notable was the sound detector produced by the American Sperry Corporation, which was based on the trumpet shape and was very precise. Since then, France has improved the parabolic type to create an inner bowl-shaped sound detector. Germany also transformed the trumpet type into an outward-opening, morning glory-shaped sound detector. However, all of the above sound detectors still had their advantages and disadvantages. After various studies, a compromise type was created. It has four narrow and long corners and looks like a box. It is easy to manufacture and has a very high efficiency. However, this type of sound detector still requires human ears to listen and determine direction. Because the feelings of the left and right ears cannot be the same, and because of mental　 (fluctuations), it is impossible to obtain accurate results. Moreover, using this device requires considerable practice, so it is difficult to meet the needs of the times. Recently, the change of sound waves into electric current has been used, and the pointer function of the ammeter is used to precisely distinguish the sound by listening, and the direction of the sound source can be determined by sight. As a result, the effectiveness of the sound detector is very great. Japan currently has 換 (replacement) sound detectors, which are the trumpet type from Taisho 14 (1925). During this Shanghai battle, the Japanese military installed them for defense in the headquarters consulate.

National Hatred, Family Hatred 4 124

— Wang Tianhen

"Cough! Danger! When did you come out? How did you leave your mother and Xiong'er?" Fortunately, we live in the same alley. I ran out of the house and saw that your front door was wide open, so I went in to close it. I saw your mother and Xiong'er standing in the living room, calling for you but you didn't respond. I called for the nanny, but she didn't respond either. I knew I couldn't delay any longer, so I pulled your mother and Xiong'er out. Because the alley entrance was bombed, we had to walk out of the back alley. As soon as we left the alley, we heard another explosion. I'm afraid our residences have all been bombed!" "Danger!," Qin Jiang said. "Even if they haven't been bombed, can we still go back now? Hurry up and find a place to hide!" the old mother said.

"I didn't even have time to tell you about my experience last night. This place is still dangerous. I need a safe place to settle my mother!" he said.

"Let's escape from Zhabei and go to the concession," Qin Jiang said very simply.

So he didn't care about his fatigue and looked for a way to run to the concession. Fortunately, Qin Jiang had a hundred or so dollars with him, so he was able to take a ferry across the Suzhou River. Everyone finally calmed down, and he had the opportunity to tell his mother about what happened overnight. His mother believed that it was the blessing of their ancestors. After he finished speaking, he continued to think about where to go. He had no money and couldn't stay in a hotel. He thought of several relatives and friends, but he knew that he couldn't stay with any of them. It was still his brother-in-law's house, where there was plenty of space, and Qin Jiang was happy to go there with him. He told his mother and Qin Jiang about it. Qin Jiang was very sympathetic. The same brother-in-law was the best. His mother was a little unwilling, but she couldn't care about so much! After arriving at his brother-in-law's house, everyone's hearts were completely at ease. But as soon as he left the dangerous situation, his patriotic fervor rekindled. He didn't feel the pain on his hands and face. After eating, everyone went to sleep, but he hurriedly went out to inquire and learned that the Chinese army had won a great victory last night. He was overjoyed! He thought: I've lived for decades, and I've never seen the Chinese army fight a foreign army! This is like a dream, the Chinese army actually won a victory! He couldn't help but want to return to Zhabei to witness the traces of victory. He completely forgot about the terror of last night.

His mother naturally disagreed with him returning to Zhabei. He said:

"We didn't bring any money when we escaped, so where will we get money to use? Fortunately, our country won the victory, and Zhabei is still our Zhabei. I'm going back to have a look to see if our house has been bombed, and I'll take the money with me."

His mother thought it was true; but it was late today, so he should go tomorrow morning. So he rested for one night, and the next morning he really went back to Zhabei. Unexpectedly, after he left, his mother waited for two days and still didn't see him return. She was very worried! On the third day, someone sent a letter, and she called Xiong'er to read it to her:

"Our house has been blown to pieces by the evil enemy. How can I not avenge the country and my family? I have decided to join the army and fight the enemy. Mother, please think of me as having already died on the night of January 28th! Fortunately, Mother is safe, and Xiong'er will soon grow up and be able to serve on behalf of your son; if your son doesn't die, he will still come back to serve. Please don't be sad or worried! I don't have much time in the army, so I can't tell you everything in detail. Your son, Zheng Hua, bows." (End)
